    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17265962159111091947"><i>El coronel no tiene quien le escriba</i> fue escrita por Gabriel García Márquez durante su estancia en París, adonde había llegado como corresponsal de prensa y con la secreta intención de estudiar cine, a mediados de los años cincuenta. El cierre del periódico para el que trabajaba le sumió en la pobreza, mientras redactaba en tres versiones distintas esta excepcional novela,</span>
  <span id="freeText17265962159111091947" style="display:none"><i>El coronel no tiene quien le escriba</i> fue escrita por Gabriel García Márquez durante su estancia en París, adonde había llegado como corresponsal de prensa y con la secreta intención de estudiar cine, a mediados de los años cincuenta. El cierre del periódico para el que trabajaba le sumió en la pobreza, mientras redactaba en tres versiones distintas esta excepcional novela, que fue rechazada por varios editores antes de su publicación. Tras el barroquismo faulkneriano de <i>La hojarasca</i>, esta segunda novela supone un paso hacia la ascesis, hacia la economía expresiva, y el estilo del escritor se hace más puro y transparente. Se trata también de una historia de injusticia y violencia: un viejo coronel retirado va al puerto todos los viernes a esperar la llegada de la carta oficial que responda a la justa reclamación de sus derechos por los servicios prestados a la patria. Pero la patria permanece muda.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17265962159111091947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/24762142-pauli-vilchez">Pauli Vilchez</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Personally I did not find the book boring at all. Is it true that is not as vivid and dynamic as the rest of GGM's literature, but I think that this b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Personally I did not find the book boring at all. Is it true that is not as vivid and dynamic as the rest of GGM's literature, but I think that this book's essence was exactly that; to describe the boredom, the hunger and the endless hope of a man who has not much else, in a context where all the things he fought for do not lo exist.<br />Also it has several different elements which makes it even better. For example, the weather is amazingly described which also seems to go with the Colonel's mood and feelings.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_2920970322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2920970322" />
    <a title="Federico DN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn"><img alt="Federico DN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478986000p2/29005117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2920970322?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Federico DN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Federico DN" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn">Federico DN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/273926.El_coronel_no_tiene_quien_le_escriba">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2920970322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12687498676253473401">A retired colonel, a small rooster, and a seventy five year patience.<br/><br/>In a desolate shantytown in the middle of nowhere, on a military controlled zone, endures with great hardships an old retired colonel. A dangerously declining health, an aging wife with recurring asthmatic attacks, a house slowly coming down to pieces, a son lost to the revolution. All his hopes are focused on the arrival of news regarding his veteran pension, that seems never to come; and a little cockfighting rooster, that se</span>
  <span id="freeText12687498676253473401" style="display:none">A retired colonel, a small rooster, and a seventy five year patience.<br /><br />In a desolate shantytown in the middle of nowhere, on a military controlled zone, endures with great hardships an old retired colonel. A dangerously declining health, an aging wife with recurring asthmatic attacks, a house slowly coming down to pieces, a son lost to the revolution. All his hopes are focused on the arrival of news regarding his veteran pension, that seems never to come; and a little cockfighting rooster, that seems to be the strongest of all three.<br /><br />A short novella about the unbreakable will of the eternally patient, and the penurious conditions of a hardly day-to-day living.<br /><br />Interesting, readable, but not exceptionally enjoyable. I've been wanting to read Gabo again for some time now; I've read a lot of his books, but this is sadly not the one I loved most. And I still have "One hundred years of solitude" on tbr. I know, unforgivable.<br /><br />Still remaining, the movie (1999).<br /><br />Until next time,<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />Un coronel retirado, un pequeño gallo, y una paciencia de setenta y cinco años.<br /><br />En una desolada villa en el medio de la nada, en una zona controlada por milirates, sobrevive a duras penas un viejo retirado coronel. Una salud peligrosamente declinante, una envejecida esposa con recurrentes crisis asmáticas, una casa cayéndose lentamente a pedazos, un hijo muerto en la revolución. Todas sus esperanzas se centran en la llegada de alguna noticia sobre la pensión de veterano que parece nunca llegar; y en un pequeño gallo de peleas, que parece ser el más fuerte de los tres.<br /><br />Una corta novella sobre la voluntad inquebrantable del eterno paciente, y las penurias de sobrevivir difícilmente día a día.<br /><br />Interesante, leíble, pero no excepcionalmente disfrutable. Hace mucho tiempo que tenía ganas de volver a leer Gabo, pero lamentablemente éste no es el libro que más voy a recordar de él. Y todavía me debo leer "Cien años de soledad". Lo sé, imperdonable.<br /><br />Queda pendiente la película (1999).<br /><br />Hasta la próxima,</span>
  <a data-text-id="12687498676253473401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13504525605605895445"><p>
  <i>‘You can’t eat hope,’ the woman said.<br/>‘You can’t eat it, but it sustains you,’ the colonel replied.</i>
</p><br/><br/>Some time towards the end of 2017, I was stuck in a bookstore café, shut in by the winter rain. And so, as boredom haunted, I picked my first García Márquez title for a light evening read to kill some time. I ended up setting sail for a never-ending voyage across the seas of Latin American literature.<br/><br/><i>No One Writes to the Colonel</i> is a short and quick read. The novella tells the story of an old co</span>
  <span id="freeText13504525605605895445" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>‘You can’t eat hope,’ the woman said.<br />‘You can’t eat it, but it sustains you,’ the colonel replied.</i>
</p><br /><br />Some time towards the end of 2017, I was stuck in a bookstore café, shut in by the winter rain. And so, as boredom haunted, I picked my first García Márquez title for a light evening read to kill some time. I ended up setting sail for a never-ending voyage across the seas of Latin American literature.<br /><br /><i>No One Writes to the Colonel</i> is a short and quick read. The novella tells the story of an old colonel and his asthmatic wife and their struggle for survival as their finances run scarce. The colonel, an old veteran of the Thousand Days' War still hopes to receive the pension he was promised some fifteen years earlier. The story is set in the period of <i>La Violencia</i> in Colombia, when martial law and censorship prevailed.<br /><br />The story was inspired by García Márquez's grandfather, who was also a colonel and who never received the pension he was promised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13504525605605895445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The novel, first published in 1961, is the story of an impoverished, retired colonel, a veteran of the Thousand Days' War, who still hopes to receive the pension he was promised some fifteen years earlier. The colonel lives with his asthmatic wife in a small village und</span>
  <span id="freeText17473851339384212718" style="display:none">El coronel no tiene quien le escriba = No One Writes to the Colonel, Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez <br />No One Writes to the Colonel is a novella written by the Colombian novelist and Nobel Prize in Literature winner Gabriel García Márquez. The novel, first published in 1961, is the story of an impoverished, retired colonel, a veteran of the Thousand Days' War, who still hopes to receive the pension he was promised some fifteen years earlier. The colonel lives with his asthmatic wife in a small village under martial law. The action opens with the colonel preparing to go to the funeral of a town musician whose death is notable because he was the first to die from natural causes in many years. ...<br /><br />عنوانها: سرهنگ کسی ندارد برایش نامه بنویسد؛ کسی به سرهنگ نامه نمینویسد؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه نوامبر سال 1984 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: کسی به سرهنگ نامه نمینویسد؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ برگردان: نسرین جهان پهلوان؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، خواجو، چاپ دوم 1361، در 104 ص<br />عنوان: کسی به سرهنگ نامه نمینویسد و تدفین خانم بزرگ؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ برگردان: جهانبخش نورائی؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، تندر، واژه، 1361، در 230 ص؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، خواجو، 1370؛ در 230 ص؛ <br />عنوان: کسی به سرهنگ نامه نمینویسد؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ برگردان: جهانبخش نورائی؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، آبگون، 1379، در 111 ص؛ شابک: 9649166882؛<br />عنوان: سرهنگ کسی ندارد برایش نامه بنویسد؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ برگردان: نازنین نوذری؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، نوروز هنر، 1389، در 95 ص؛ شابک: 9789647109475؛ <br />عنوان: کسی به سرهنگ نامه نمینویسد و چند داستان دیگر؛ نویسنده: کابریل گارسیا مارکز؛ برگردان: اسماعیل قهرمانی پور (شمس خوی)؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، روزگار، 1389، در 197 ص؛ شابک: 9789643742102؛ چاپ دوم 1392؛ <br /><br />داستان، روایت روزگار سرهنگ پیری ست، که سال‌ها، در انتظار رسیدن نامه‌ ای از سوی دولت، به سر می‌برد، تا برای شرکت و خدماتش، در یک جنگ داخلی بسیار قدیمی، مبلغی به عنوان مقرری برای او، در نظر گرفته شود. سرهنگ، در حالیکه، در شرایط بسیار وخیم مالی قرار دارد (همانند شرایط مارکز در حین نوشتن اثر)، تصمیم دارد، تا با مقرری مورد انتظار، علاوه بر ترتیب دادن یک زندگی آبرومندانه، برای خود و همسرش، خروس جنگی پسرش را، که چند ماه پیش در حین توزیع مخفیانه ی اعلامیه‌ های ضد دولتی، کشته شد، خود پرورش دهد. انتظار او برای دریافت نامه ی مزبور، ادامه می‌یابد، و آن نامه، هرگزی به دستش نمی‌رسد. او که به پیروزی خروس جنگی، به چشم نوعی انتقام مرگ پسرش، نگاه می‌کند، در شرایط سختی قرار می‌گیرد، انتخاب راهی میان زندگی سخت بین: حفظ و پرورش خروس برای انتقام، یا فروش خروس برای ادامه ی زندگی. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1848197709" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1848197709" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1848197709?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141032535" href="/book/show/2644376-no-one-writes-to-the-colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1848197709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15019531390150115262">I was stuck without a book at my relatives' house today. Fortunately, they were readers, so rooting through their bookshelves I found this novelette by Marquez which I had not yet read. Talk about serendipity.<br/><br/>This is a short story set in the familiar magical realism universe of Aureliano Buendia and the land of Macondo from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude' title='One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel García Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Hundred Years of Solitude</a>. However, there is no magic here: it is the brutally realistic tale of the unnamed "colonel" and his wife, who live in penury in the all-too-fam</span>
  <span id="freeText15019531390150115262" style="display:none">I was stuck without a book at my relatives' house today. Fortunately, they were readers, so rooting through their bookshelves I found this novelette by Marquez which I had not yet read. Talk about serendipity.<br /><br />This is a short story set in the familiar magical realism universe of Aureliano Buendia and the land of Macondo from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a>. However, there is no magic here: it is the brutally realistic tale of the unnamed "colonel" and his wife, who live in penury in the all-too-familiar dictatorship of a South American nation. Their son Augustin has been killed by the authorities for distributing seditious literature. The colonel and his wife eke out their days, pinning their hopes on the military pension which should arrive any day; and the fighting cock owned by their son, which would hopefully prove to be the champion, when the cockfight season arrives. However, the exigencies of existence and his wife's constant nagging makes the colonel contemplate the unthinkable - sell the cock to the bloodsucking trader Sabas. But there is still time - and as the fighting season arrives, the colonel recovers his dignity in the utter depths of shame.<br /><br />This small novelette is very rich in metaphor which talks to the reader at many levels. The colonel, waiting for the letter every Friday which would announce his pension but is always doomed to disappointment ("No one writes to the colonel," as the postmaster says) is the quintessential tragic hero albeit in modern non-romantic garb. The fighter cock is the symbol of his fast-fading dignity, also the last thing to memorise their son by; its sale to the rapacious capitalist is the last nail in the coffin of the proud manhood of a class. Indeed, the cock, as Augustin's friends insist, does not belong to the colonel alone but to the country as a whole. Metaphors of sickness abound: the colonel's perennial stomache problem, his wife's asthma, and the severe diabetes of the trader Sabas. The dreariness of the atmosphere is compounded by the incessantly falling rain.<br /><br />Vintage Marquez, in short.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15019531390150115262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2496760192?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nishat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nishat" href="/user/show/36859595-nishat">Nishat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140157499" href="/book/show/859844.No_One_Writes_to_the_Colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2496760192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1183592046376517269"><i>His eyes fell upon other eyes exactly like his own. </i><br/><br/>A deeply moving tale of an enduring marriage. The colonel and his asthmatic wife are rotting alive. Bereaved of their only son, they are left to eke out a living in so repressed a town that it becomes increasingly difficult for the aging couple to preserve some sense of dignity. <br/><br/>As the colonel, every Friday, without fail, awaits a letter regarding his pension, which never arrives, and the wife appears always on the verge of a brutal asthma atta</span>
  <span id="freeText1183592046376517269" style="display:none"><i>His eyes fell upon other eyes exactly like his own. </i><br /><br />A deeply moving tale of an enduring marriage. The colonel and his asthmatic wife are rotting alive. Bereaved of their only son, they are left to eke out a living in so repressed a town that it becomes increasingly difficult for the aging couple to preserve some sense of dignity. <br /><br />As the colonel, every Friday, without fail, awaits a letter regarding his pension, which never arrives, and the wife appears always on the verge of a brutal asthma attack, they watch their love grow old and bodies wither away amidst the rampant moral corruption and hopelessness of their surroundings.<br /><br />In a society where voices, if ever raised, are persistently silenced, Márquez has weaved an intriguing tale, revolving around this elderly couple endeavoring to defend their honor and that of their deceased son. The colonel and his wife, although extraordinarily defiant during the hardest of times, are relatable, and their grief remarkably palpable. Simplicity is unquestionably the strength of this heartfelt tale.<br /><br />In the middle of the novella, the colonel acknowledges with sadness, <i>"All my comrades died waiting for the mail."</i> It is the same with the colonel. He will wait until death devours him too. Heartbreaking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1183592046376517269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1342081309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342081309?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barry Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barry Pierce" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce">Barry Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20804833-no-one-writes-to-the-colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342081309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9175315942112208276">In this incredibly short novel, Garcí­a Márquez tells the story of an elderly and senile Colonel who, every Friday, waits to receive his pension in the post. However, he's never received his pension. Not once in fifteen years. Both the Colonel and his wife live in destitution in a small village in war-torn Colombia. They grieve the death of their son and try to sell off their belongings in order to continue living. <br/><br/>This is an utterly pessimistic novel. The Colonel and his wife are living hopeles</span>
  <span id="freeText9175315942112208276" style="display:none">In this incredibly short novel, Garcí­a Márquez tells the story of an elderly and senile Colonel who, every Friday, waits to receive his pension in the post. However, he's never received his pension. Not once in fifteen years. Both the Colonel and his wife live in destitution in a small village in war-torn Colombia. They grieve the death of their son and try to sell off their belongings in order to continue living. <br /><br />This is an utterly pessimistic novel. The Colonel and his wife are living hopeless lives and in this hopelessness, Garcí­a Márquez thrives. Nothing happens in the novel. There isn't a beginning or an ending. Like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24695317.Leaf_Storm" title="Leaf Storm by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaf Storm</a> we are dropped into the middle of a story. We are observers of the Colonel and we can't help him. <br /><br />This is a really fantastic little story and shows are clear improvement in the structure and story problems I found in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24695317.Leaf_Storm" title="Leaf Storm by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaf Storm</a>. Take me away Gabo! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3171811672" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3171811672" />
    <a title="Tamoghna Biswas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97513431-tamoghna-biswas"><img alt="Tamoghna Biswas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580746459p2/97513431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3171811672?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamoghna Biswas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamoghna Biswas" href="/user/show/97513431-tamoghna-biswas">Tamoghna Biswas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141032535" href="/book/show/2644376-no-one-writes-to-the-colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97513431-tamoghna-biswas?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97513431-tamoghna-biswas?shelf=magic-realism">magic-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97513431-tamoghna-biswas?shelf=gabriel-garcia-marquez">gabriel-garcia-marquez</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3171811672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11384253407203767901"><b>
  <i>"The colonel took the top off the coffee can and saw that there was only one little spoonful left. He removed the pot from the fire, poured half the water onto the earthen floor, and scraped the inside of the can with a knife until the last scrapings of the ground coffee, mixed with bits of rust, fell into the pot."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Thus began the tale that, though nothing special(<i>probably</i>) is still very close to my heart. And that's not just because Márquez considered this as his best one, so much so he wrot</span>
  <span id="freeText11384253407203767901" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"The colonel took the top off the coffee can and saw that there was only one little spoonful left. He removed the pot from the fire, poured half the water onto the earthen floor, and scraped the inside of the can with a knife until the last scrapings of the ground coffee, mixed with bits of rust, fell into the pot."</i>
</b><br /><br />Thus began the tale that, though nothing special(<i>probably</i>) is still very close to my heart. And that's not just because Márquez considered this as his best one, so much so he wrote his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener"> One Hundred Years of Solitude</a> just to ensure people read this one, if only in reference. Not because I found a reference to it in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4392.Living_to_Tell_the_Tale" title="Living to Tell the Tale by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener"> Living to Tell The Tale</a>, where he said the colonel is inspired from Márquez's own grandfather.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"It is very important to bear in mind that fundamental to this novella, as also to all great literature, is its polysemic nature. That is, the artist imbues it with many senses and many meanings..."</i>
</b><br /><br />You won't find, probably anything unique about the tale. A geriatric Colonel who along with his wife live in a post-war military governed region (probably after <b>
  <i>La Violencia</i>
</b>), desparately, yet patiently awaiting the arrival of his pension letter, for fifteen monotonous years. They have no source of income and the meagre savings they have are mostly spent pence by pence on the rooster, whom the Colonel is raising for a cock-fighting match. The Colonel is also way too proud to depend on burrowing, however harsh the circumstances may be. And the novella surrounds around this; so you can gather there's no definite plot-line, despite how closely it touches your heart.<br /><br />But the story is different from what Márquez is generally known for. It's not a tale on magic realism, ( there is only one relevance and you will remember the legendary Colonel Aureliano Buendía). Many stories are there that delineates poverty, but I have read very few(in foreign language to me, I mean) that does it so skillfully. Also it's dubiously melancholic and optimistic with many metaphors, without being over dependant on symbols. The Colombian critic, Hernando Téllez, has said, for example, that <i>a fundamental characteristic of the book is the simplicity of its design, almost the ease with which the reader can go from episode to episode in the book.</i><br /><br />So, all in all, that's it. It's not for you if you want to read something eventful or alike. But don't read it thinking it a side material to Márquez's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener"> One Hundred Years Of Solitude</a>, for it's not.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"'Everything's that way,' she whispered. 'We're rotting alive.' And she closed her eyes so she could concentrate on the dead man."</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11384253407203767901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer10194102281360348443"><br/>★★★★ Stars<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23875.El_coronel_no_tiene_quien_le_escriba' title='El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>El coronel no tiene quien le escriba</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23875.El_coronel_no_tiene_quien_le_escriba' title='El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1167484006s/23875.jpg' alt='El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>One of my goals this year is to go back to reading some books in my mother language. This novella by well-known Colombian writer <i>Gabriel Garcia Marquez</i> seemed like a great place to start.<br/><br/>As a young woman growing up in Latin America, Marquez's Magical Realism was at least in part what ignited my passion for reading. Eventually I moved on to other genres, but reading this short novel reminded me why he remains one the continent's most beloved and c</span>
  <span id="freeText10194102281360348443" style="display:none"><br>★★★★ Stars<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23875.El_coronel_no_tiene_quien_le_escriba" title="El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">El coronel no tiene quien le escriba</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23875.El_coronel_no_tiene_quien_le_escriba" title="El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1167484006s/23875.jpg" alt="El coronel no tiene quien le escriba by Gabriel García Márquez" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>One of my goals this year is to go back to reading some books in my mother language. This novella by well-known Colombian writer <i>Gabriel Garcia Marquez</i> seemed like a great place to start.<br><br>As a young woman growing up in Latin America, Marquez's Magical Realism was at least in part what ignited my passion for reading. Eventually I moved on to other genres, but reading this short novel reminded me why he remains one the continent's most beloved and celebrated authors.<br> <br>Although this particular story is less magic and more realism, you would recognize Marquez's poetic and detailed-oriented style. <br>Some of his well known characters, such a Colonel <i>
  <b>Aureliano Buendía</b>
</i>(protagonist of his best known novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel García Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a>), as well as the fictional village of <i>
  <b>Macondo</b>
</i>, make cameo appearances but they are not the center of the narrative.<br><br>Marquez wrote <i>No One Writes to the Colonel</i> while living in exile in Paris during the late 1950's. It tells the story of an unnamed impoverished colonel, who, after 15 years of retirement, continues to wait for a letter from the government that will finally grant his rights as a veteran of the 1000-day Colombian war. <br><br>They are nights when the colonel and his wife go to bed hungry, but even while experiencing so much deprivation, he insists on feeding the rooster inherited from their deceased son. The rooster comes to dominate the daily life of the couple and his final fate is an essential part of the plot of the story.<br><br>For the colonel receiving his hard-earned benefits go beyond fulfilling his financial needs, is a matter of pride, an acknowledgement of the sacrifices he made for his country. <br><br>This is a sad story and the author leaves it to the reader to imagine what happens at the end and whether the letter ever arrives, but I think is a good introduction to Marquez's legendary style of writing.<br><br>*********************************************** <br><br>I listened to the Spanish version of this audio book. Actor Diego Trujillo was the perfect choice as narrator. Trujillo, who is originally from Colombia, used his natural inflection to successfully convey the flavor and tone of this novel. <br><br><br><br><br><br><br> <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10194102281360348443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14395132423153988638" style="display:none">"The only thing that comes for sure is death"<br />-Gabriel García Márquez, No one writes to the colonel<br />🌼<br />Fifteen years have passed since the Thousand days war ended in Columbia, and the colonel is still waiting for his letter of pension to arrive which was promised after the war.<br />Struck in poverty, the old man lives with his wife, the couple had lost their only son, lives off by selling little objects around the house and now they are just left with an old clock and their son's rooster.<br />🌼<br />How long before they break down? How long can the Colonel keep off not selling the rooster in hope of winning the cockfights?<br />🌼<br />The prose is extremely eloquent and the tale really rich albeit a small one. The aura of a South American town which sets the background of the whole story has an enchanting factor of its own.<br />The tale has an undertone of melancholy all throughout, but at certain points, that's the beauty of it.<br />I heard this is not the best works of Marquez but I thoroughly enjoyed the short read and can't wait to dig deeper into his works.<br />🌼<br />Genre: contemporary, fiction, short-stories, south-american literature, classic <br />Rating: ⭐⭐⭐.5/5<br />Reading difficulty: ⭐⭐⭐/5</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcy" href="/user/show/3526621-marcy">Marcy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96628766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14004894251566413525">I read this book when I was in high school and despite my young age I really like the psychoanalysis. The obstinate Colonel of the anticlerical Cristeros War keeps waiting for the pension that has been promised to him but never delivered. Every Friday, he goes down to the docks, dressed in his best suit in anticipation of the arrival of the letter announcing his pension. Everyone knows that he is waiting in vain, but he refuses to face reality, even though, deep in his heart, he knows that the l</span>
  <span id="freeText14004894251566413525" style="display:none">I read this book when I was in high school and despite my young age I really like the psychoanalysis. The obstinate Colonel of the anticlerical Cristeros War keeps waiting for the pension that has been promised to him but never delivered. Every Friday, he goes down to the docks, dressed in his best suit in anticipation of the arrival of the letter announcing his pension. Everyone knows that he is waiting in vain, but he refuses to face reality, even though, deep in his heart, he knows that the letter will never arrive. His wife is suffering from asthma; their son Agustin was killed by the fascists; and the roof over their head will soon be taken away because of the unpaid mortgage. Yet the Colonel stands by his dream, refusing to give up despite poverty and hunger. He knows that if he lets go, there is nothing else left. It's true that you can't eat hope, but it's also true that it keeps you alive!! Dignity and pride are human values that can't be bought. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14004894251566413525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_58809936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58809936" />
    <a title="Lamski Kikita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1439240-lamski-kikita"><img alt="Lamski Kikita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321835207p2/1439240.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58809936?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lamski Kikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lamski Kikita" href="/user/show/1439240-lamski-kikita">Lamski Kikita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330256872" href="/book/show/1208596.No_One_Writes_to_the_Colonel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mia, polyana</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58809936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12120418027953761295">Those who say that Gabo's best works are his short stories are not mistaken. How can anyone but him recount the history of a nation, an ideology, and a whole continent in under 70 pages?<br/><br/>The colonel and his wife have no names in the book, because they are the main charachters that represent everyone in the era in which tyranny ruled over most of Latin America, leaving those who valued their country the most, more than empty handed.<br/><br/>How sad is it to wait for what you deserve, every friday, for 15 y</span>
  <span id="freeText12120418027953761295" style="display:none">Those who say that Gabo's best works are his short stories are not mistaken. How can anyone but him recount the history of a nation, an ideology, and a whole continent in under 70 pages?<br /><br />The colonel and his wife have no names in the book, because they are the main charachters that represent everyone in the era in which tyranny ruled over most of Latin America, leaving those who valued their country the most, more than empty handed.<br /><br />How sad is it to wait for what you deserve, every friday, for 15 years (well, over 40 years actually)? The colonel really makes me think of alot of people everywhere around the world who have been waiting for that little sum of money that will feed them for a week...that cash that will repay all their debts and save face. <br /><br />The most important part of this story, to me, is the fighting rooster which belonged to their murdered son. Rooster fights are a normal activity in South America, and it's not the frowned-upon thing that most people see as animal cruelty in other places. This rooster is both hope and burden, because even though it might bring cash in in January, it needs to be fed until then...while the colonel and his wife starve.<br /><br />I do not know what other people think the rooster represents, but maybe because of a personal refernce, i felt that this rooster represents one's ideals and political beliefs, in an age when everything is changing. The rooster is the last thing the colonel has, and so are his ideals after everyone else either left or sold out (like his rich friend Sorin). The way the world has become, how toug life is, the pressures from people around you and from your loves ones, make you feel that your only choice is to sell the rooster; you are older now, no time for idealistic thoughs, or else how are you going to put food on the table? This rooster represents all what you fought for your whole life, the blood of your comrades and the sacrifices of your people, all that have been lost, unappreciated, and forgotten...this is the last remnant of an era. But how will you sustain it? how will you feed it under the watching eyes? how will you save it from those preying on it? is it worth the risks and agony and feverish nights?<br /><br />will you face the fact that <i>humanity does not progress without a price<i></i>? or will you save it, never sell it, and eat...well...shit?</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12120418027953761295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2041246161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041246161" />
    <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread"><img alt="WhatIReallyRead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483674713p2/52500467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041246161?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WhatIReallyRead" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread">WhatIReallyRead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/39797522-el-coronel-no-tiene-quien-le-escriba">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=owned-ebook">owned-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=hispanic-literature">hispanic-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=bilingual-edition">bilingual-edition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=read-in-spanish">read-in-spanish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041246161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10398634191326025774"><b>In case you were wondering, no one really did write to the Colonel.</b> This was book #3 of my Español-a-thron.<br/><br/>The main character, who remained nameless throughout the whole book, became a Colonel at age 20. It's been 56 years since then, and in that space of time the Colonel "has done nothing remarkable". <br/><br/>He and his asthmatic wife have been living off of their late son's money, but that came to an end. There is nothing left to sell in the house, no source of income and no one to turn to for help. T</span>
  <span id="freeText10398634191326025774" style="display:none"><b>In case you were wondering, no one really did write to the Colonel.</b> This was book #3 of my Español-a-thron.<br /><br />The main character, who remained nameless throughout the whole book, became a Colonel at age 20. It's been 56 years since then, and in that space of time the Colonel "has done nothing remarkable". <br /><br />He and his asthmatic wife have been living off of their late son's money, but that came to an end. There is nothing left to sell in the house, no source of income and no one to turn to for help. They are starting to starve. The only valuable thing these two have left is the fighting cock which belonged to their late son. The Colonel doesn't want to sell him, seeing the solution to all of their problems in a military pension which he is waiting to receive. He's been waiting for it for fifteen years, checking for mail weekly and getting nothing. <br /><br />He is uncompromising, absolutely unbending in his belief that he will one day receive the pension, even though there is no reason to think so. <b>And because of that stubbornness, he doesn't look for ways to save himself from starvation. </b>His wife starts out mutely compliant, resolute and dignified, but by the end of the book, their conflict comes to the surface. She sees how delusional and destructive his behavior is, and he brings her down right along with him. <br /><br /><b>Marquez masterfully painted the hardness of Colonel's character and the bleak situation around him.</b> I felt really sorry for the wife and felt absolutely no compassion for him. Apparently, the Colonel thinks that being in the military 56 years ago is enough for him to be supported for a lifetime, so much so that he refuses to lift a finger to provide for himself. Why hasn't he ever acquired any skill or profession to earn money in that space of time? But he is indignant and even after 15 years of rejection doesn't consider for a minute that things won't go his way. A despicable character. <br /><br />It was a good book :) Off to the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10398634191326025774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_703503425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/703503425" />
    <a title="El Avestruz Liado" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13116552-el-avestruz-liado"><img alt="El Avestruz Liado" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392233881p2/13116552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/703503425?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El Avestruz Liado" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El Avestruz Liado" href="/user/show/13116552-el-avestruz-liado">El Avestruz Liado</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer703503425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7351144634380935708">While <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude' title='One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Hundred Years of Solitude</a> might be his most celebrated work, I have always felt that García Márquez is at his top in his short novels. This and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23878.Chronicle_of_a_Death_Foretold' title='Chronicle of a Death Foretold by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chronicle of a Death Foretold</a> are at least to me his most enjoyable novels by a wide margin.<br/><br/>Briefly, this is the story of a colonel, his asthmatic wife and a rooster who belonged to their assassinated child. Superficially a history of false hopes this is actually more about turning closed eyes to reality, to rely on memories of "better times" (</span>
  <span id="freeText7351144634380935708" style="display:none">While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a> might be his most celebrated work, I have always felt that García Márquez is at his top in his short novels. This and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23878.Chronicle_of_a_Death_Foretold" title="Chronicle of a Death Foretold by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" rel="nofollow noopener">Chronicle of a Death Foretold</a> are at least to me his most enjoyable novels by a wide margin.<br /><br />Briefly, this is the story of a colonel, his asthmatic wife and a rooster who belonged to their assassinated child. Superficially a history of false hopes this is actually more about turning closed eyes to reality, to rely on memories of "better times" (which can be the past or an invented future) instead of facing the pains of life in a forsaken moorland.<br /><br />Since this is a short novel and there are already a gazillion reviews of it already I'll stop the review here. Go for it, it is a great lecture that seems to flow in slow time and has an ending that will stay with you for a while. </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Aashna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/119128608-aashna"><img alt="Aashna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596134596p2/119128608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3468720605?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3468720605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11714826390090213761">I picked up this book because I wanted the satisfaction of reading a book in one sitting, and also a dear friend recommended this because it was bound to make me feel "cursive". <br/>To me, the story of the colonel is about longing and poverty and dignity. I found myself wanting to understand his principles of life a little better, and constantly hoping for luck to strike. <br/>Definitely a book I shall re-read on a train ride soon (once the pandemic ends and train rides are permissible by law).</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2940490213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2940490213" />
    <a title="Vartika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63883678-vartika"><img alt="Vartika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601807242p2/63883678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2940490213?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vartika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vartika" href="/user/show/63883678-vartika">Vartika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141032535" href="/book/show/2644376-no-one-writes-to-the-colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2940490213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6100040708934641490"><i> No One Writes to the Colonel </i> is a novella by Gabriel García Márquez, set in the fictional town of Buendia and Macondo during the Ten Year Colombian Civil War. All the magic-realism of <i> One Hundred Years of Solitude </i> is stripped down to the impossible reality that Márquez describes in his 1982 Nobel Prize Lecture: one that is so brutal, it seems unbelievable to the outsider; one that belongs to Latin America. <br/><br/>The story is about an ageing colonel, who waits his days out in hope for the military </span>
  <span id="freeText6100040708934641490" style="display:none"><i> No One Writes to the Colonel </i> is a novella by Gabriel García Márquez, set in the fictional town of Buendia and Macondo during the Ten Year Colombian Civil War. All the magic-realism of <i> One Hundred Years of Solitude </i> is stripped down to the impossible reality that Márquez describes in his 1982 Nobel Prize Lecture: one that is so brutal, it seems unbelievable to the outsider; one that belongs to Latin America. <br /><br />The story is about an ageing colonel, who waits his days out in hope for the military pension promised to him finally arriving after fifteen years of waiting. He lives in abjection and penury with his ailing, asthmatic wife; raising a rooster in memory of their son, Agustín, who was killed at a cockfight for distributing clandestine newspapers. The couple sustains their lives in hope for the pension letter for the colonel's service in the Thousand Days' War — now overdue for fifteen years — and the fighting cock; owned by their deceased son and kept in his memory; winning the prize. But poverty and old age prove insufferable, and the colonel — edged on by his wife — grapples with the question of whether to sell the cock to the rich Sabas for money, or to keep his dignity and wait for death. <br /><br />As all of Márquez's tales, meaning in this novella runs deeper and more metaphorical than it seems. One can almost tell from the very beginning that the colonel would not recieve his pension — he is nameless, and as insignificant in the country as the animal he tries to feed. Living under censorship and martial law, he has nothing but pawned possessions dwindling hope to live on:<br /><br /><blockquote> <i> 'You can't eat hope', the woman said. 'You can't eat it, but it sustains you,' the colonel replied. </i> </blockquote><br /><br />The temptation to sell the rooster — the only tangible memory of his son — possibly stands for the sale of Latin American nations to a faulty capitalism, but sickness pervades: the colonel feels 'fungus' and 'flora' growing in his stomach — something parasitical gnawing away at life —; his wife's asthmatic breathing fills the house; even the rich, greedy trader, Sabas, is dying of diabetes, symbolic excess. <br /><br />Márquez; himself a journalist; also comments on the spirit of the citizens amidst censorship to 'pass on' the real news of war in the interiors of Colombia; while catholic religion — in the form of Father Angel — reinforces the oppressive censorship and condemns those who disobey it: the bell tolls twelve times, and all movies are unfit for everybody. <br /><br />The unbelievable corruption and faulty legal system are highlighted by the painfully slow processing of the colonel's claim, the disappearance and killings of party rebels, and the lawyer's insistence that a certain document — an important proof — can be all but forgotten about, never to be found. <br /><br />Deeply poignant and reflective of long-drawn suffering, <i> No One Writes to the Colonel </i> echoes the postman's statement every Friday, and injects it with its real meaning for Latin America: that people do not matter. In fact, the novella opens with the death of a musician which the colonel seems important because it is the first death from natural causes in ages. <br /><br />Ultimately, the colonel refuses to sell the rooster, and finds out wears the dignity he finds in his of shame:<br /><br /><blockquote> <i> 'And meanwhile what do we eat?' she asked, and seized the colonel by the collar of his flannel night shirt. She shook him hard. <br /><br />It had taken the colonel seventy-five years — the seventy-five years of his life, minute by minute — to reach this moment. He felt pure, explicit, invincible at the moment when he replied: 'Shit'. </i> </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6100040708934641490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97695678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97695678" />
    <a title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly"><img alt="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349701607p2/2190636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97695678?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly">Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97695678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7395936079006103206">The colonel is 75 years old. His wife is about the same age and suffers from continuous asthma attacks. He himself is not in good health. He constantly feels something odd inside his stomach and would have high fever in the evenings. The couple are starving.<br/><br/>As a former military man he has applied for, and is supposed to receive, a pension from the government. So every Friday he goes to their town postman hoping to receive a letter informing him that he'll finally receive his long-awaited pension</span>
  <span id="freeText7395936079006103206" style="display:none">The colonel is 75 years old. His wife is about the same age and suffers from continuous asthma attacks. He himself is not in good health. He constantly feels something odd inside his stomach and would have high fever in the evenings. The couple are starving.<br /><br />As a former military man he has applied for, and is supposed to receive, a pension from the government. So every Friday he goes to their town postman hoping to receive a letter informing him that he'll finally receive his long-awaited pension. But each and every time he receives nothing. He has been waiting for 15 years already. But no one writes him anything.<br /><br />The country is under martial law. Nine months before, their grown-up son, their only child, was shot while distributing subversive leaflets inside a cockpit.<br /><br />The couple had sold almost everything they have except for a picture (which no one will buy), an outdated clock and a fighting cock their son left behind. But even the latter would starve for days as they don't have money to buy corn for it. When their son's former companions gave corn for the cock, some of it the colonel's wife cooked for their meal. Their house and lot are on the verge of being foreclosed for unpaid debts.<br /><br />Their only sources of hope: that the pension may now arrive and that the cock would win come January during the cockfights when the owner of a fighting cock, if it wins, is entitled to 20% of the winnings even if he didn't place any bet. But these are big IFs. And there are also big WHAT IFs: what if the pension does not arrive? What if they're force to sell the fighting cock before the cockfight in January (the story started in October and ended sometime December)? What if the cock dies? Or loses during the fight?<br /><br />The colonel knows these too. And while he's still surveying those faraway hopes that keep him alive, his wife asks him: "And meanwhile what do we eat?" She seized him by the collar of his shirt and shook him hard:<br /><br />"It had taken the colonel seventy-five years--the seventy-five years of his life, minute by minute--to reach this moment. He felt pure, explicit, invincible at the moment when he replied:<br />"'Shit.'"</span>
  <a data-text-id="7395936079006103206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_772918071" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772918071" />
    <a title="Marc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2876105-marc"><img alt="Marc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569160429p2/2876105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772918071?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc" href="/user/show/2876105-marc">Marc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140157499" href="/book/show/859844.No_One_Writes_to_the_Colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2876105-marc?shelf=latin-american-literature">latin-american-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772918071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10819510855752222744">This story is clearly a prequel on "100 years of loneliness". Marquez hasn't painted yet his exuberant world here, but the ingredients are the same: a 75-year-old colonel, who leads a desolate life with his wife, especially since his son was murdered; he has been waiting for his pension for 15 years; every Friday he visits the postmaster in vain; the only hope rests with the cock of his son who might win a big prize in cockfighting. Nonsense, absurdity and inhumanity predominate in this short st</span>
  <span id="freeText10819510855752222744" style="display:none">This story is clearly a prequel on "100 years of loneliness". Marquez hasn't painted yet his exuberant world here, but the ingredients are the same: a 75-year-old colonel, who leads a desolate life with his wife, especially since his son was murdered; he has been waiting for his pension for 15 years; every Friday he visits the postmaster in vain; the only hope rests with the cock of his son who might win a big prize in cockfighting. Nonsense, absurdity and inhumanity predominate in this short story. Didn't really resonate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10819510855752222744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3414866538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3414866538" />
    <a title="Ankita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20524419-ankita"><img alt="Ankita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601883300p2/20524419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3414866538?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ankita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ankita" href="/user/show/20524419-ankita">Ankita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140157499" href="/book/show/859844.No_One_Writes_to_the_Colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3414866538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer835203997782795206"><br/>"You can't eat hope, but it sustains you"<br/><br/>Colonel is colossally patient. He hopes for a mail that would airlift his worries. He hopes that his son, Augustin's rooster would kick it all in the upcoming fight. He hopes that his corrupt politician friend, Sabas, would help him. He hopes that his ailing wife would understand why he is pining his hopes onto a rooster<br/><br/>No One Writes to the Colonel is a novella about a retired Colonel and his asthmatic wife and their life in a martial law imposed country.</span>
  <span id="freeText835203997782795206" style="display:none"><br />"You can't eat hope, but it sustains you"<br /><br />Colonel is colossally patient. He hopes for a mail that would airlift his worries. He hopes that his son, Augustin's rooster would kick it all in the upcoming fight. He hopes that his corrupt politician friend, Sabas, would help him. He hopes that his ailing wife would understand why he is pining his hopes onto a rooster<br /><br />No One Writes to the Colonel is a novella about a retired Colonel and his asthmatic wife and their life in a martial law imposed country. The revolutionary Colonel has been waiting 15 years for his prized possession i.e. his pension. He is, thereby, forced to sell hi personal belongings to make the ends meet. <br /><br />The context is based on the Civil War that happened between conservatives and liberals in Colombia. The central theme here is hope and its lack thereof. The Colonel and his wife have hope over more than a decade for something that is rightfully there's to come about. Another aspect is the quashing of basic rights by the Government, when the Govt fails to take care of him after he gives up (rather forcefully) fighting with the rebels. It adds that his son too died passing off inflammatory anti Government messages in one of the rooster fights. Marquez subtly brings in the political wisp.<br />The story ends with Colonel saying SHIT. Funnily enough, I was hoping for cliffhanger (IDK why!). Marquez manages to mingle different themes intricately. As we move, we are rooting for the Colonel, we understand his wife's point too but we can't (or atleast I could not) really take a side. </span>
  <a data-text-id="835203997782795206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141032535" href="/book/show/2644376-no-one-writes-to-the-colonel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8549273-sunny?shelf=1315-read">1315-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8549273-sunny?shelf=all-boxall">all-boxall</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319299070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8961581539651877506">This story is on THE LIST, but the only English version I could find in my library was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77338.Collected_Novellas' rel='nofollow noopener'>in this book of collected novellas</a> which contains three stories, including this one.<br/><br/>I decided to skip ahead and read this story, and then, if I really, really liked it, I'd read the other two. But, I'm returning the book to the library with the other two stories unread. I hate the stigma that goes with a two star rating. As if it means I didn't like it. But, it just means I thought it was OK.<br/><br/>The Colonel and hi</span>
  <span id="freeText8961581539651877506" style="display:none">This story is on THE LIST, but the only English version I could find in my library was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77338.Collected_Novellas" rel="nofollow noopener">in this book of collected novellas</a> which contains three stories, including this one.<br /><br />I decided to skip ahead and read this story, and then, if I really, really liked it, I'd read the other two. But, I'm returning the book to the library with the other two stories unread. I hate the stigma that goes with a two star rating. As if it means I didn't like it. But, it just means I thought it was OK.<br /><br />The Colonel and his wife are old and sick and poor. The Colonel was promised a pension at the end of the War (apparently the Thousand Days' War, of which I've never heard) but the pension still hasn't come through. Fifteen years later, the man still goes to the post office every Friday hoping for the letter announcing his pension will start, only to be disappointed every week.<br /><br />It's a sad story, one that evokes feelings of despair, pity, outrage. But, I just don't think the story was as powerful for me as it could have been. Unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7244.The_Poisonwood_Bible" title="The Poisonwood Bible by Barbara Kingsolver" rel="nofollow noopener">The Poisonwood Bible</a>, which prompted me to google=research the Congo Crisis, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/128029.A_Thousand_Splendid_Suns" title="A Thousand Splendid Suns by Khaled Hosseini" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Splendid Suns</a>, which prompted me to google=research the Russian invasion of Afghanistan - well, this book just didn't pique my curiosity. (Yes, I did actually search for the Thousand Days' War, but only so I could include it in this review.)<br /><br />So, yeah. The book - it was OK.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26416859-calzean?shelf=author-columbia">author-columbia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26416859-calzean?shelf=culture-colombia">culture-colombia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26416859-calzean?shelf=nobel-prize-winner">nobel-prize-winner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1653621178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5099234194902394035">One of the most saddest books I have written.<br/>A 75 year old ex-Colonel lives in Macondo, destitute and starving. His wife has asthma. Every Friday he waits for a letter that will bring with it his pension for his role in the civil war. The letter never comes. <br/>They are in mourning for their son who has been killed by authorities.<br/>They own nothing except the fighting rooster they inherited from their son. The Colonel constantly dithers between selling the rooster or putting the rooster into the ring</span>
  <span id="freeText5099234194902394035" style="display:none">One of the most saddest books I have written.<br />A 75 year old ex-Colonel lives in Macondo, destitute and starving. His wife has asthma. Every Friday he waits for a letter that will bring with it his pension for his role in the civil war. The letter never comes. <br />They are in mourning for their son who has been killed by authorities.<br />They own nothing except the fighting rooster they inherited from their son. The Colonel constantly dithers between selling the rooster or putting the rooster into the ring. He dithers about everything. he worries more about dignity than being able to feed himself and his wife.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5099234194902394035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4ogNSE01WwR0LD9MOUEUkf/s99apum59TG8zN1dgX83DgV4w63TEw7Tvm6igKf18fnFHaI/2o2uP/xkGxEl4YQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ca4QT51GVvNjIaX7r0+ORWrefKuocLZToSw23/J8dKQop0M3OwfJNKPiAR82J2eo60PMFY48e0VivBzuYVVTCA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
